The "Sign a Fraternal Friend" Campaign, which extended from January 1. 1987 to December 31, 1987 is now in the history books. We should all be proud of our accomplishments. We set goals of 30 million dollars in new insurance and we exceeded that goal by nearly 9°/o We sold $32,659.454.00. We only have had one year better than this. 1986, when we sold $36,753.494.00 If we stop and think back, only five or six years ago we were selling only five or six million in new insurance We should all be proud. Four hundred and seventy (470) of our members recommended new business. Some sold 252 policies and others only sold one. But remember, we needed all of you to make the 5,125 new sales Thank you all! WEDNESDAY, FEBRUARY 17, 1988 A Jtenotuned Slovak Violinist Peter Michalica to Perform at Illinois Benedictine College The renowned Slovak violinist. Peter Michalica. and accompanist, Cheryl Wampler. DMA. will appear at Illinois Benedictins College on Saturday. February 20, 1988 A discussion series beginning at 7.00 p,m. and a recital at 8:00 p.m. will lake place in Benedioline Hall Sodel Center. Tickets for adults are $7 00. and for senior citizens and nonIBC students, S4.00. Violinist Pete'r Michalica is one of the most prominent contemporary representatives of Slovak performing art. He has al hi® disposal a nch fund ol natural musicality, talent, and sharp intellect. He was a, prize winner at the Carl Flesch Intemáíi?5nw-Aít^n Competition in Lon- doQ.ip J^rS. He was awarded the Slovak National Pnze in 1982 and the title "Distinguished Artist of Slovakia" in 1986. Peter Michalica studied at the Conservatory and at the College of Musical Arts m Bratislava. Slovakia, with Professor J. Skladaný:' He did his postgraduate Wqrk^aťMoscoWs P.l. Tchai- kowski Conservatory with “Professor V. Yankelevitch from 1971 to 1974 In 1975 he was invited by Professor A. Gertler to continue his post-doctorate studies at the Royal Conservatory of Music in Brussels, Belgium. During this period he won the "Premier Prix avec Grand Distinction" in the competition organized by the Royal Conservatory. The recital is being run by the Cultural Affairs Committee of Illinois Benedictine College. It is in commemoration of the centennial of Illinois Benedictine College and in recognition of the ethnic heritage ot the college. Alo|z L. As we all know, a more professional, businesslike field force must be developed for our system to survive. In order to develop recommenders properly and train your future supreme officers, our sales managers should: 1) Have been a steady producer (not necessarily a large producer).. 2) Be witling to become an F.LC, 3) 4) 5) 6) 7) 3) Be willing to continue education (seminars, workshops, or other schools). Be able to devote at least 20 hours per month to field supervision. Have a valid slate insurance license, if required. Be a resident ol area supervised Have non-grating personality and a healthy share ol tact Be a member of the Society RESPONSIBILITIES ot A DISTRICT MANAGER The responsibilities of the Distnct Manager are divided into three areas: 1) Production — Under the.direclion of the Vice-President and Marketing Director. 2) Administration — Under the direction of the Executive Secretary and Chief Auditor... du 3) Fraternal — Under the direeffim of the Executive Secretary and Fraternal Director. Duties under Production: I) See that branches have capable officers. This is the most important job 2) Be personally familiar with all branch officers It is easier to get feedback if the comradery is good. 3) See that a'l officers ate knowledgeable about the products we sell 4) Help develop sales techniques so that branch officers can sell larger policies more easily. 5) Aid officers in district sales 6) Hold meetings so people can exchange ideas 7) Make use of the Marketing Director 8) Recruit new officers for branches before needed. 9) Do no! liquidate branch if we lose the town. This is the Iasi resort. 10} Do not let branches deteriorate to where they must be liqisdated or merged 11} Help Marketing Committee institute and run contest to aid production. 12) Encourage goals in your aisirict. 13) Maintain enough annual premium increase to support his'her salary. 14) Discourage pooling of busmess so that eacn recommender gets proper compensation and recognition for his/her work 15} Accept no compensation except tram Home Office 16) Make necessary reports as requested by Vice-President or Marketing Director. Duties under Administration: 1) See that all branch officers operate branch in accordance with directions of Executive Secretary 2) See that branch has a copy of al! curreni forms and destroy all outdated . ones. 3) Be thoroughly familiar with all branch numbers especrsliy in your district 4) District Manager 'will be notified of any delinquent branch under his/her supervision, and he/she is expected to take appropnate action. Duties under Fratemallsm: 1) Help all branches with their social and religious activities 2) Ask branch officers of active branches to help with your fraternal program 3) Work with Fraternal Director to promote new fraternal activities 4) Get every branch active in seme fraternal field. 5) Make sure your home branch s doing well so you can use it as an example. Terminations District Sales Managers performance shall oe reviewed and evaluated annually For failure to perform ther duty, they shall be terminated The Distnct will then be requested to submit three new names to the Vice-President. KRAJSA, KSGG OPINIONS ABOUT JEDNOTA CONVENTIONS Jozef Husek: “O našich, za našich” (About Our Own, for Our Own) (Joseph Husek was the Editor of JEDNOTA for some 37 years tn the early part of this century. In the spring of 1926 a series of articles by Husek. entitled "O našich. za našich" (About Our Own. for Our Own), appeared la the JEDNOTA. These articles openly discussed the problems and opinions of the Conventions of the First Catholic Slovak Union. We present here one of the articles In the series that appeared In the May 26. 1926 Issue of the JEDNOTA. -Editor) "After my own opinions, the greatest ;A^^rqyer of our organization is too much per- politics. True, there might be other (flings, but I do not know about them. To fight against this destroyer or wrecker is like beating your head .against the wall. ' Such a thing controls our conventions. The conventions are run and controlled by this politics. Nowhere does one hear the proverb, silence is golden.' as at our conventions. Whoever goes to the convention with some personal ambition is wise to lock up his mouth, or if he speaks, he'd better not say the whole truth because he will not get any thanks for it. "For what reasons do we call conventions? Do we call them to elect officers, to amend bylaws and to listen to reports from the officers? All of this we could do in one day. or two at the most. In some reports we hear good recommendations or advice. But often the officers read them and no one is concerned. Time flies and the work remains. All the time the delegates arc interested in only campaigning. These petty politicians then call extra meetings in the evening. And there they "elect” officers, criticizing the old ones, in a word, making fun of them behind their backs. "At the regular convention sessions they are quiet because the individuals attacked would be defended and exonerated. They accuse. Judge, and sentence without hearing from the accused. This is so because their accusations. and charges are baseless and frequently malicious. "Such things are done at our conventions to honorable people. And at these meetings they bargain and intrigue. The petty politicians come together and decide things on political slates. Surely at the selection of officers they do not decide according to character or particularability. but more so according to the interests of some individual or group. "From these circumstances it Is impossible to expect complete impartiality, even for the president. To be a president of a convention is a difficult one. especially if he is also a candidate for the presidency of the organization. He must be very careful not to anger anyone. For the debates that happen at a convention are verbose, get sidetracked, and usually end Indecisively. "The roll of demagogy at our con ventions is not a small one If the existence of our Jednota was hanging on a thread, if it had to decide whether it was going to continue or not. the petty politicians, and also those against their better judgment, would organize the membership against the only means with which the organization might defend itself against destruction. "I do not have any hope of completely eliminating this personal politics from our conventions. because if we closed all the doors behind us. this would creep into the room through the keyhole. But we could at least try honestly to repair the harmful effects of this activity to some degree. Our conventions must be more productive and constructive." Washington Letter Beyond the Rhetoric on Contra Aid By Laorie Hansen WASHINGTON (NC) - Before a key vote on contra aid Feb. 3. supporters and opponents of continued military assistance piled high their conflicting sets of evidence on atrocities allegedly in Nicaragua. U.S. politicians, a Catholic bishop exiled from Nicaragua and heads of religious orders offered contradictory reports of tactics being used in the 6-year- old war and speculated openly on what sending more aid to the Nicaragua rebels would mean for the future of the Western Hemisphere. The lengthy and heated debate was played out on the House floor, from the Oval Office. tn Capitol Hill press conferences. at street demonstrations and on the editorial pages of newspapers. Bandied about were weighty themes including Justice, peaceful resolution of conflict, religious and political freedom and the right to self-determination — themes that could have been pulled straight from U.S- bishops’ pastoral letters or homilies given at Sunday Mass. The only thing both sides seemed to agree upon was that the stakes were extremely high. The American public was left wondering who and what to believe. On one hand there was President Reagan insisting Feb. 2 that continued contra aid was an "insurance policy" necessary to keep pressure on Nicaragua's Sandinista regime to move toward democracy and away from regional subversion. There was exiled Nicaraguan Bishop Pablo Antonio Vega calling the current Sandinista government of Nicaragua "communist" and charging that religious persecution has become public policy in his Central American homeland. The bishop of Juigalpa Prelatuře. who now resides in Miami. said cutting the aid would threaten the "unity” of the Americas. On the other hand. Auxiliary Bishop P. Francis Murphy of Baltimore said at a press conference that continued U.S. military assistance would "disrupt the delicate peace process In the region and therefore . . - continue the untold suffering (Continued on Pago 5) LIGHT ONE CANDLE It Is belter lo light one candle than to curse the darkness. (Christopher Motto) By Father John Catoir Director of The Christophers THE BISHOP Bishops in our contemporary American environment are stretched by their office almost beyond human limits. It's clear to anyone who has faith that they do not live out their commitment on their own strength alone. They have special supernatural help. A bishop is an apostle of Jesus Christ, but he is also a business administrator, a law enforcer, a religious leader, a symbol of unity, and a dozen other things. He must balance all of the above in such a way as to be a good shepherd and a caring pastor to his people. Without extraordinary’ grace, good health, and a sincere desire to serve, his Job would be humanly impossible. As a businessman, he is chief executive officer of a federation of corporations and is responsible for their fiscal solvency. Personnel management alone is a full-time preoccupation. As law enforcer he is a moral watchdog who must be above reproach himself, decisive In protecting orthodoxy, and firm in carrying forward sometimes unpopular policies. As a religious leader he has to Inspire loyality. He must also relate diplomatically to civil authorities, encourage Interfaith relations and lead his people lo positive, constructive social acton. His first and most essential task, as an apostle of Jesus Christ, is to lead his people in the worship of God. This means he is more than a follower of Christ, he is a devoted disciple, one who sits at the feet of the Master, drawing from His strength and wisdom. As a symbol of unity and transcendence, he serves as a Christ figure, in Lhat role he must try to be a good shepherd, one who feels his lambs with the good news that God loves them deeply. Some bishops are specialists at business, some are not. Some are holy, some are not. But most, by God’s grace, are able to balance this impossibly complex Job with dignity and poise. How? The Holy Spirit, of course. Is the source of their strength and their Joy. The bishops who are really remembered, however, are the ones who. In spite of the enormous pressures of daily life, arc able to communicate love. Because they are loving human beings, they bear rich and abundant good fruit in their lifetime. Illusions and Realities THE SOVIETS IN VENICE By Michael Novak VENICE — From this city, it is said. Robert Benchley once cabled to the New Yorker: "Arrived Venice. All streets flooded. Please advise." Before and since, visitors to Venice have been stunned by the two powers that rule tills city: by nature, everywhere circumambient and lapping literally at every’ doorstep, and by civilization, elegantly floating on slight and invisible foundations. In few places are both powers to be observed in equally precarious equipoise. Six years earlier than a thousand years ago. in 982. a Benedictine monastery was built on St. George’s Island in Venice, a city that had already known Christianity for more than half a millennium. The Venetians say that culture's center is cult: that from a core worship civilization flows, and politics and art spring. So it is that the CINI Foundation deliberately established Itself in 1951 in this ancient Benedictine monastery on Si. George's. The Foundation seeks now to help Venice to extend its tradition of openness to east and west, north and south. As walers surround the land masses of ihe earth, so Venetians feel connected on their own water to every part of earth. An inquiring, curious, and seeking people, they have even named their airport for Marco Polo. It is altogether fitting, then, that in 1988 (amid the cold winds of February that slap the green water against the sides of boats, and against the piers) the CINI Foundation and the Region of Venice hosted a special conference on human rights. They invited all 35 participant nations of the all-Europe Helsinki Accord, including the Soviet Union and its Marxist allies, both at ambassadorial levels as well as private citizens from each. And. perhaps because 1988 marks the 1000th anniversary of the extension of Christianity as far north as FROM OUR JEDNOTA HISTORY By Anthony X. Sutherland. Pb.D. JEDNOTA FRATERNALISM - 1926 STYLE Probably the most admirable chapters in Jednota's long history are those which contain acts of genuine fratemalism. those benevolent works performed out of Christian char ity and one's loyalty to the principles of the First Catholic Slovak Union. Whether it was a collection for a funeral, aid to students, or the care of widows and orphans, the real meaning of Jednota fratemalism was demonstrated. Let's look at just a few examples from the year 1926. In September 1926. the First Catholic Slovak Union had its XXII Convention in Scranton. Pa., and as at previous conventions. people in need of help or aid of some kind petitioned the delegates or appeared in person At this 1926 meeting. John Kroll, armless since birth, appeared before the delegates on a stage to ask for some funds in order to go to school and become self-sufficient. That same evening a passing of the hat yielded over $100 from the delegates. Next, a cripple, Michal Suchar, was carried in onto the stage to petition for help. He also received aid. Eight students received some support to continue their studies and several religious orders and institutions received amounts ranging from $100 to $500 to carry on their work. These are only a few examples from this convention. Only a few weeks earlier, in August 1926. there was an even greater opportunity to demonstrate fratemalism. A mine disaster in the small town of Clymer. Pa., at a mine owned by the Clearfield Bituminous Coal Corporation, claimed 44 lives including several Slovaks. As had happened so many times in the past, the great Jed- notar. Andro Novak, went into action. The following morning at 4 00 a m . Novak left Pittsburgh with Jan Sabol, arriving in Clymer at 8:00 in the morning. The men learned that four members of Branch 563 in Clymer had been killed: Michal Misenko from Lubotiny In Saris: Juraj Lastz: Stefan Pjura and Jan Pjura. both from Gro- mos in Saris. Misenko left a wife and 8 children: Juraj Lastz a wife and 5 children: Stefan Pjura. a wife and 5 children; and Jan Pjura. a wife and 12 children — a total of thirty children. Novak and Sabol, together with the officers of Branch 563. Jan Potocek and Stefan Papcun. saw to it that these survivors were taken care of during this crisis. Novak and Sabol went to the undertaker to see that all the funeral arrangements were in order. The pastor of the Catholic church in Clymer. Rev. Fabian Kondrla. a member of Jednota, should also be commended for his help during this tragedy. He was so exhausted from work on the day of the disaster that he was unable even to talk to Novak and Sabol when they ar rived. Kondrla was well respected by all the people of the community. Under his direction all able bodied men of the town dug the 44 graves for the victims. Examples such as these can be multiplied many times over throughout the history of the First Catholic Slovak Union. In the future we will relate more stories of true Slovak fráter- nalism. " Kiev, they chose to concentrate on ihe theme of religious liberty. Everyone senses that the moment is a fragile one. Under Gorbachev’s reforms, the Soviet Union is precariously — perhaps momentarily — open to some new experiments in the direction of a virtue beloved of Venetians: openness to the . world, and perhaps especially. 3 to a few tentative and partial concessions to religion. What was distinctive about the conference at St. George’s ’ was the simultaneous presence of Soviet officials and Soviet J dissidents; Polish officials and fl a Paris-based representative of / Solidarity; and religious leaders from the Russian Orthodox. Roman Catholic. Uniate. Protestant. Jewish, and Islamic faiths, as well as ambassadors and dryly secular sociologists. Most remarkable were exchanges between Ihe Soviet officials and those they have never before had to talk to । across a table, such dissident emigres as the literary critic. Vladimir Maximov, and the original Helsinki Monitor. Alexander Ginzburg, now living in Paris. Two years ago. the Soviets would never have attended such a conference: so said their attending ambassador Moreover. their lone here was determinedly. almost pleadingly, accommodating. "We ask you to help us." one said. Their overall message had three $ parts: in the past, we made ' many errors regarding human rights: in the present, not all is yet well; in the future, you can be sure reforms now begun will continue, irreversibly. As usual, of course, the Soviet message comes with a hint of pent-up aggression. Much more gently than usual, the Soviet ambassador showed J that he could and would, if pressed, attack the failings ol^ the West regarding "economic rights." such as unemployment. homelessness, etc For 40 years now. the Soviets have claimed that their recognition in law of "economic rights" makes them morally superior to the West, narrowly fixed on Individual rights. Soviet ambassadors have been known to say. further. as 1 myself heard at the Human Rights Commission in Geneva in 1981 and 1982: "Individuals do not have rights: only states have rights." Western rebuttals on these points have grown sharper in , recent years, as the conference al St. George s again showed. The actual practice of "economic rights" in Ihe USSR and . Eastern Europe is inferior not only to Soviet theory’ but also to Western practice. Even the Soviets do not claim that they will actually be able to have homes for all their people until at least the end of this century. What they in theory call "rights” they in practice treat as (often far off) "goals." Moreover, it is becoming harder for the Soviets to take part in dialogue such as this without conceding more and more lo individual rights, to the dignity of persons, and even to conscience. These words (especially the last) have not yet crossed official Soviet lips, but the Soviet search for respecti- bility and ihelr own admissions of past errors arc driving them down a "slippery slope" toward just such unmentionables. They seem visibly to feel this. Many al the conference — especially the representatives of persons In the USSR still suffering in prison for acts of conscience — report that, since Iasi August the Gorbachev reforms have clearly been slowed. No doubt many in the Soviet hierarchy see — and fear, and arc determined to resist — a slide down that "slippery slope." Venice has seen the rise and fall of many empires and systems of belief. A citadel of í i republican experimentation. It is a symbol of age-old trust in civilization, against all odds. Americans give strong credence to the values of peace, stability, order and Justice. "Americans are faced with the choice of how do you accomplish these things best: Do you fight communism with weapons, or by bringing about a more just society and eliminating the cry for social change by bringing about social change?" said Quigley. His suggestion to U S. Catholics attempting to shape their own opinions on the issue is to look beyond the rhetoric of "those who say either that Nicaragua is about to become the cat's paw of the Soviet Union as it seeks to conquer the rest of the hemisphere and move up through Texas, or those who say the kingdom of God has come with the Sandinista revolution." He said U.S. Catholics are asked to weigh carefully the arguments with which they are presented and make "prudential judgments." Exercising prudence will be a challenge as the Arias peace process unfolds and President Reagan and his political opponents begin to oiler their own assessments of whether the plan's conditions arc being met. REALM OF SLOVAK GENEALOGY 'A FAMILIAR TIME FRAME" By Ray Plutko (EDITOR S NOTE. Thrs xs the fifth in a senes ol feature articles dealing with the realm of genealogy it is one specifically designed lor Slovak descendants and is so structured to serve as an introductory course for the novice, meet the needs of the advanced researcher — or. il nothing else, the curious. Today s feature — A FAMILIAR TIME FRAME ) It is surprising just how similar our differences are. There is an interesting pattern developing by those of you seeking added assistance from our Slovak Genealogy Research Center Tins trend centers on the topic of "terminology" and as it relates to the geography of Slovakia It is easy to see why a number of you are experiencing problems in your work and with this m mind, it might be worthwhile to share your dilemma with others Initially, one must develop a con- sdousawareness of a time frame when Conducting research This is particularly important when making use of a map and/or utilizing archive material It was very common in Eastern Europe for boundary lines to change due to continuous wars and treaties With these shifts in boun daries. often times the name ol the nation would change and tn some cases, a new one would be created Thus, before attempting genea- togtcal research in Eastern Europe it is ot vital importance to identify the locality from which a particular ancestor immigrated and/or what language he/she spoke poor to leaving the native Country. Keep m mind, there were many Slovaks who also spoke Hungarian This is an excellent clue to a region of present-day Slovakia upon which to locus in order to place matters rn pro per perspective. there was no official place as Slovakia prior lo 1918. With this introduction, nere are a few terms which are a must for your research and geographic vocabulary AUSTRO HUNGARIAN EMPIRE — Political and military term used to identify a large mass o' land m Cen tral and Eastern Europe, one which was the dominating force in the area from roughly 1000 to 1918 AD Within this territory, there were numerous nationalities and languages. one of these being Slovak — not to mention accompanying land the majority of what is now present-day Slovakia. AUSTRIA - Present-day nation bordering Slovakia on the southwest and one dominated by the Hapsburg Dynasty throughout much of history It reached <ts greatest size prior to World War II. with Vienna the capital city HUNGARY - Name of another present-day country, but one which has been interwoven into Slovak history lot centuries. It borders most of Slovakia on Ihe south where ma jor segments of land were lost in 1918 at the close of World War I Ironically, these basically represent the same lands taken from the original Slovak tribes in the tenth century and for years was known as Upper Hungary " This is a term you may stumble upon in conduc ting your research The term Lower Hungary " refers to the land which basically comprises present- day Hungary BOHEMIA - The westernmost sector ol land which comprises Czecho-Slovakia Although there are Slovaks reading m this area, the vast majority of people are proper ly identified as Czech MORAVIA — The middle sector ol land which separates Bohemia from Slovakia and is also pan of present day Czecho slovakia Once again, the majority ol people are Czech, but there are numerous Slovaks employed and living in this segment of land. SLOVAKIA — The eastern sector of land and third such area which, collectively comprise present-day Czechoslovakia The capital city is Bratislava and it is this land of which the major segment ot our research will be concentrated. FEBRUARY- L7. 1988 A- POPE’S LENTEN MESSAGE, 1988 Dear Brothers and Sisters in Chnst, In a spirit of joy and hope, I wish through this Lenten Message to exhort you to do penance, such as will bnng you the abundant spiritual fruits of a more dynamic Christian life and a truly effective charity. Lent is a period which profoundly affects the life of every Christian community: it fosters a spirit of recollection, prayer and attentiveness to the Word ol God: it encourages us to respond gener- ouslyJfo-^J^Lo.rd's call as ex- preMed^lhe^Nords of the Pro- pheb fc riot this the tact lhal I choose ... to share your bread with the hungry, and bring the homeless poor into your house? ... Then you shall call, and the Lord will answer, you shall cry. and hs will say 'Here I am' " (Is. 58: 6.7.9) Lent 1988 occurs during the Manan Year, on the eve of the third millenium of the birth of Jesus, our Saviour. Contemplating the divine motherhood of Mary, the woman who bore the Son of God within her womb and surrounded the child Jesus with special care and love, J am reminded of the painful drama of so many mothers, whose hope and ;oy have been shattered by the early deaths of their children. Yes. my Brothers and Sisters. I ask you to think of this scandal of infant mortality, which claims tens of thousands of victims every day. Children are dying before their birth; others have only a bnef and painful existence which is cut short by diseases that could easily be prevented. Il has been clearly demonstrated that in the most severely poverty-stricken counInes of the world it is the children who have the highest death rate due to acute dehydration, parasites, polluted water, hunger, lack of vaccination against epidemics, and even the lack of love. Under conditions of such poverty, a great many children die in their infancy, white the physical and psychological development of others is so seriously affected that their very survival is threatened, and they are at a disadvantage in finding a place for themselves in society. The victims of this tragedy are the children who are bom in a state of poverty which too often stems from social injustices as well as their families who do not have the resources they need and who are wounded forever by the early deaths of their children. Recall with what determination our Lord Jesus demonstrated his solidarity with children: he called a small child to himself, set him in their midst and declared: “Let the children come to me" (Mt. W:2,5; 19:4). I strongly urge you. in this liturgical period ol Lent, to allow the Spirit of God to take hold you. to break the drains of selfishness and sin. In a spirit of solidarity. share with those who have fewer resources than yourselves. Give, not only the things you can spare, but the things you may perhaps need, in order to lend your generous support Io the actions and projects of your local Church, especially to ensure a just future for children who are least protected. By so doing, dear Brothers and Sisters in Christ, your charity will ' shine forth, and people will "see ; your good works and give glory to your Father who is in heaven“ (Mt. 5:16). During Lent, following the example of Mary who faithfully accompanied her Son to the Cross, may • our faithfulness to out Lord and our- generous deeds bear witness Io our obedience lo his commandment! With all my heart, I bless you. in Ihe name of the Father, and of the Son. and of the Holy Spirit. Amen, Church on Cutting Edge of Efforts to Solve World Problems (Continued from Page i) In less than a week, the pope met with two Centra) Amencan churchmen who are official mediators in Ihe civil wars in their respective countries, with Nicaraguan President Daniel Ortega. Honduran Foreign Minister Carlos Lopez Contreras, and Jordanian King Hussem. He was also scheduled to meet Egyptian President Hosni Mubarak Feb. 5 In Central America, Cardinal Miguel Obando Bravo of Managua is mediating between the Nicaraguan government and U.S.-backed guerrillas; and Archbishop Arturo Rivera Damas'of San Salvador is mediating between the Salvadoran government and Marxist-oriented guerillas. The pope encouraged this kind of activity during a 1983 Central American trip, citing the moral principle that Christians must be reconciling forces in wartorn societies. It is a natural rote for the church in Central America where Catholicism is the majority religion and where the church has been a major social force for the past 500 years. Since 1983. however. the pope has been relative“ ly quiet, letting the Central American church leaders take the lead in hammering out concrete peace plans. The pope continued his low-key approach after the January meetings He Jet Ihe cardinal and the archbishop do most of the public talking. They spiced their support tor a regional peace plan with pointed criticisms of some of the main players in the region s political problems Cardinal Obando Bravo told the United Stales to freeze aid to the Nicaraguan guerrillas, called contras. as long as the government moves, toward democracy. Aid to the contras continues as a cornerstone of President Reagan's Central American policy, despite the regional peace plan signed by the five Central American presidents opposing outside aid to warring factions and despite strong opposition by the U.S. Congress. But the cardinal also told the Nicaraguan government to move faster toward "an authentic democ racy” by establishing a general amnesty and by holding genuine presidential elections which would guarantee the transfer of political power if the Sandinista candidate lost. Tne pope reiterated the cardinal’s pleas to Ortega, asking him to move toward a "true democracy." a code phrase often used by Nicaraguan critics to indicate a lack of government desire to establish a Western-style democracy Archbishop Rivera Damas blamed Salvadoran guerrillas as the main obstacle to negotiations in his country, saying they are looking for excuses not to sit down at the bargaining table He also named the Nicaraguan and U.S. governments as reluctant to follow provisions of the Central Amencan peace plan Regarding the Middle East, the pope scheduled meetings with Hussein and Mubarak, both moderate Arab leaders and proponents ol an international conference to resolve the problems in Israeli- occupied territories. The meetings were scheduled during prolonged bloody conflicts in the occupied territories between Israeli troops and rock-throwing Palestinians. The disturbances left at least 38 dead by the time Hussein and the pope met Feb. 1. International criticism, including from the pope, already had been heaped on Israel lor his harsh measures against demonstrators. The Vatican used the Hpssein meeting to reiterate its specific goals, based on the moral principles ot human dignity, justice and religious freedom The goals are: — Peace and security for Israel — A Palestinian homeland. — An internationally guaranteed status for Jerusalem as a holy city open to Christians. Moslems and Jews. All three goals have been politically elusive and controversial since the founding m 1948 of the modern state of Israel in what was then Arab-ruled Palestine. The first two are considered mutually exclusive by many of the Mideast’s political forces and the third puts the Vatican at odds with Israel’s 1980 unilateral declaration ol Jerusalem as its capital. East Jerusalem and the Iraeli-occupied West Bank previously were under Jordan s rule Christianity is a minority religion in the area, so Catholic leaders do not have the influence they have in Central America lo take on mediating roles. But at the same time, the pope wants the region's leaders to know that the church has a rote to play and specific positions lo defend Vatican Adds Concern for Families Austere Policies MANILA, Philippines (NC) — The poor will suffer most from austere economic policies adopted to repay the Philippines' $28 billion debt, according to the report of a Philippine Jesuit agency. The Institute on Church and Social Issues said government economic stabilization policies “hava neglected to consider their impact on the poor and most vulnerable groups in society, an impact which can have severe and permanent detrimental effects.” Titled “The Cost of Ihe Foreign Debt on ihe Poor; A View trom the Philippines." the report recommends that future policies be formulated to ensure that basic needs of the poor are fulfilled. 2nd Sunday of Lent, 1988 A Lenten Reflection (Continued from Page 1) The Gospel according to St. Mark describes the Transfiguration and the Apostles' failure to understand Ihe significance of this event and Jesus' words of what it meant "to rise from the dead." Since Jesus is portrayed as the Suffering Messiah, the Transfiguration is a sign of what is to come, namely, the resurrection of the Lord. Inc., Southampton, PA. The phenomenon — called by researchers "failure to thrive" syndrome — has emerged because many parents mistakenly believe their children will become obese or develop ätherosdero- ss as adults. They think that using fowl at dairy products and very lean meat will lessen this risk. Researchers and pediatricians at Cor- risen Irie of Christ, we must undergo renunciation, suffering and death. No matter what stage of life we are in. the Lord calls us to new opportunities to be with him and usually this requires a great sacrifice, sometimes even pain. But in the end there is triumph, The last phrase of the song, "The Old Rugged Cross," sums it up well: "I will cling to the old rugged cross and exchange it someday for a crown." nell University found, in a study cl children exhibiting “fažure to thrive” symptoms that parents often curial snacks and, in all. provide less food to the young child These researchers .noledjhat young children were consuming less than 75 percent of the calorie requirements for th»r age groups Hpwever. these researchers led by Michael Pughese. M.D.. Cornel’ School of Medicine, cited parents may be "overly concerned." since a number of other factors besides early feeding practices — such as heredity — may be involved. Experts agree that children have certain nutrition requirements, and need certain amounts of lat and calories for normal weight gain and complete brain development. They say that, generally, proper childhood growth necessitates consumption of protein including eggs, dairy products, and red meat. They also recommend that, beginning at age 5. calones from fat in a ybung child's diet should compose between 30-40 percent of total calories. To improve young children's diets. Cornell researchers working with "failure lo Ihrive" children recommended substituting whole for lowfat dairy products, increasing the amount of food offered at mealtime, and offering snacks between meals. Once these recommendations were implemented, improvement was seen, and the young children resumed normal growth patterns. Pugliese suggested that each family can continue further implementation of the recommendations accortíng to individual case histories and family background. If there is heart disease or obesity in the family, tne parents should consul their pedatricran or family physician for specific dietary recommendations. Il is widely accepted among nutritionists that a balanced diet from the four basic food groups — milk. meat, fruit arid vegetables, and grains — is essential for children’s proper growth and development Going by the four food group approach is a convenient way for many people to assess the adequacy of a diet. Nutritionists’ usually advise, says Dairy Council, that small children should have two-three servings a day from (he milk group, two from the meat group, at least four from the fruit/vegetables group, and four from the grains group — with some whole grain products included. Regain Dignity WASHINGTON (NC) - Cardinal Bernard F. Lav/ ol Boston at a March for Life vigil Mass in Washington urged a respect for life that includes "every human person" and that moves the nation to regain its Jost sense ol Ihe dignity of all. Preaching al the Mass at the National Shrine of the Immaculate Conception. he stressed that respect for each person must encompass the unborn. tlie terminally ill. Ihe homeless. AIDS patients, the mentally ill. drug and alcohol abusers and anyone whose life has been diminished by illness, poverty or a broken family brother Abel? — and its official completion date. Dec. 27. the feast of the Hc-ly Family. The word "family " accompanies . nearly every mention of the homeless in the document, in contrast to some UN. publications on the same topic where the word does not appear at all. in an accompanying tetter, the pope invokes ths image of Jesus born in a manger and the Holy Family as refugees in Egypt. Tne document declared that the home “is rooted in the sacrament of marnage" for Christians As the text suggests, the trauma homelessness wreaks on families is universal. In Eastern European couniries. such as Poland, housing shortages mean marriage is postponed or families are forced to share cramped quarters indefinitely — despite a state monopoly on building construction. In the West, building speculation, high rents and lagging construction hinder young couples seeking a home of their own. Apartments in the city center of Rome, for example, are left empty m a silent landlord protest against strict rent control laws, while the city’s homeless population is rising. And in metropolises as diverse as Lagos. Nigeria. Sao Paulo. Brazil. and Jakarta. Indonesia, entire families may be forced to Jive in a single room or shanty. Tnese situations are "serious obstacles" to the right, to found a family, the homeless document said. When a young couple is forced to live with their parents or shoulder the burden ot high rents, it can have "negative consequences" for the new family, the document said. "It is not rare that the first years of married life are conditioned by such exterior factors that result in an almost forced delay in having children.” the document concluded. Surprise Meetballs J4 lb. twice ground beef i see cup dry bread crumbs 16 cup 7-Up * 5^ tsp. garlinc salt tsp. onion salt 24 small stuffed green olives Combine beef. egg. bread crumbs, 7-Up, and seasonings. Place 1 tbsp, of meat mixture into palm of hand and flaten; place an olive into center of meat and mold meat around olive. Place meatballs 2 inches from broiler and broil for 6 to 3 minutes, turn once. Insert a toothpick into each meatball and serve hot. Makes 24 meatballs. Maple Coconut Drops cup maple syrup >4 cup shortening, melted 1 egg, beaten W cup milk cups sifted, enriched flour 2 tsps, baking powder 14 tsp. salt >4 cup shredded coconut Combine maple syrup and melted shortening. Stir in beaten egg and milk. Mix and sift flour, baking powder, and salt Add gradually, mixing well. Stir in coconut. Drop by teaspoonfuls on greased baking sheet. Bake in moderate 350° F. oven 12 to 15 minutes. Cool. Frost with melted semisweet chocolate and coconut. .Makes 3 doxen. Royal Plum Pudding 1 pkg rasberry gelatin Dash salt Dash ginger % tsp. cinnamon 14 tsp. cloves 1J4 cups boiling water cup raisins % cup currants % cup chopped dates 14 cup mixed candied fruits 1 flat can crushed pineapple, drained 1 cup chopped pecans Whipped cream Combine gefatin, salt, ginger, cinnamon. and cloves. Pour water over mixture and stir until dissolved. Add raisins and currants. Chill until slightly thickened and fold in remaining fruits and nuts. Turn into a 3-CUp mold and chill until firm. Garnish with whipped cream forced through a pastry bag. Makes 5 to 8 servings. Oven-Bag Roast Chicken 2 to 4 lb. broiler-fryer 1 tbsp, flour 2 tbsps. melted butter 4 celery strips Salt and pepper Preheat oven to 350° F. Shake flour in small size (10 x 16-inch) Brown-in- Bag and place bag in 2-inch deep roasting pan. Place celery strips In bottom of bag (prevents chicken skin from sticking while cooking). Rinse chicken and pat dry; brush with melted butter, season with salt and pepper. then place in bag on top of celery. Close bag with twist tie; make 6 ^-inch silts in top. Cook 1 hour or until tender. Makes 4 to 6 servings. Cheese Souffle 14 cup butter >4 Cup flour 1 tsp. salt ■ 4 tsp. dry mustard 1'4 cups milk 2 cups shredded American cheese 6 eggs, separated Melt butter In top of double boiler over direct heat Blend In flour and seasonings and heat until bobbly. S4SS lilia ť.tOl am •■ ms? •••k i, e»|j »ua Vl«0- T3”t 111,101 FOREIGNERS INVESTING IN THE U.S. The increased involvement ol foreign investors in the U.S. real estate market over the past few years has helped keep mortgage rates more moderate than they might have been without foreign investments, as well as keeping the interest rates lower, according to the latest study by real estate experts In addition, commercral/induslrial markets in several areas, particularly m the oil producing regions of the country, have been bouyed up by foreign investors stocks and mortgage-backed secuntees helped contribute to an additional 800.000 sales of homes or housing complexes in 5986 The study finds that the coastal regions of the U S. are mo-e oopuiar invest ment sites to foreign investors than the interior of the country, with over 51 percent of the office space in the central business ehstnet of Los Angeles owned by foreign investors, compared to only about 10 percent of Chicago's business distnct being owned by foreigners. Experts predict, however, that as foreign investors become better acquainted with the U 8 market, they will come (o invest in central areas as well as the coastal cities. The predominate nationally o’ foreign investors in many oties is Japanese, however, there is a mix of Europeans. Middle Easterners and Canadians m several cities For instance, there are majorities made up of Canadians in Chicago and Eun> peans In Washington. D.C. Foreign investors, the study reports, tend to keep their real estate holdings longer than Ihe average American investor, feeling that such properties are a safe haven for capital and offer plentiful long-term yields Since U S properties are seen in such a favorable long-term light, many foreign investors are more likely lo pay premium prices tor investment opportunities than their Amencan counterparts The normal real estate investment transaction with foreign investors is one m which a Simple deal is made with 50% to 100% down, with financing obtained from outside the U.S. Since foreigners consider investment in American properties a longterm proposition, they are also less likely to close transactions as qu ckly as many American investors Foreign investments in the U.S. leaped from $11.4 bill on In 1984 to S21.2 in 1986 This vast increase is due. experts say. to the large and diverse U.S. market and a higher rate of return on U.S. properties than on properties in many investors’ homelands. In addition. America has one of the most stable governments in the world, highly skilled labor force. and a relatively less strict tax system .■ Many people, not familiar with the current investment market m the country, w feared that foreign investors were 'taking over America." However, foreign investors, the study shows, make up less than one percent of Ihe nation's tangible assets For many markets, the impact of increased foreign investments has meant the difference between stagnation and a fairly healthy market. In honor of our beloved Father McKoy, I welcome this opportunity m the name of our Sisters to offer our tribute Io him as he has so often offered his Io us in such a life-giving and love giving way Father Charles Patrick McKoy was born on June 14. 1920. the youngest child ol Alice and John McKoy of Garfield (Pittsburgh). The McKoys belonged to Si Lawrence O'Toole Parish and it was hero that Charles attended elemenlary school, going on to complete his high school education at Central Cafhohc from which he graduated in 1937. Amidst a solemn and festive celebration with the Precious Blood Fathers, his family and friends. Father Charlie, as he was affectionately called, offered his life so that others may be enriched by Christ and was ordained to the priesthood in Carthagena, Ohio, al St. Charles Seminary, in the Cincinnati Province of the Order, on December 10. 1944 Left to right: Hefene Cincebox. Rev. Edward Zavelí, pastor of St. Mary Magdalene’s, and Helen Baine Helene and her many artifacts — 4 tables! . As a Minister of Ged. he was appointed an assistant pasior m both th.e Diocese ol Richmond. Va.. and Steubenville. Ohio. He spread the Good News ol tire Gospel as a Navy Chaplain for three years, serving the Mannes in Japan and in North Carolina. An Open Letter of Response Sharing the integrity of his faith and his love for his neighbor. Father McKoy s praying and preaching took him to many areas of the United States and to other parts of the world as he served in his Congregation's Mission Band, including the Air Force bases m Morocco. Libya, North Africa. England. Germany. Bermuda, and Puerto Rico He was a good shepherd to all God s people everywhere After those years of ministry, he willingly accepted Io serve at St. Edward's Parish in Cleveland, Ohio, lor three years On June 10, 1971. Father Charlie was asssgned as Chaplain to the Mothernouse of the Vincentian Sisters of Chanty. However, this was not our first contact with him. Our community had previously become acquainted with him through fruitful and happy retreat experiences Certainly, though in 1971, he was welcomed with joy to be among us on a more permanent bass. On numerous occasions he made it quite clear to the visiting clergy that hinted that they were interested m hrs job that the position of the VSC Chaplain was not available as long as he could help it It was with high regard that he spoke ol and for our community For that, we Vincentian Sisters of Chanty are most appreciative and grateful We befeve that he will still be interceding (or us as he walks m' 'newness of tile' - hopefully on the greens that he loved so much' During his 17 years of chaplaincy, he genuinely enjoyed his daily prayer ministry with our senior Sisters He preached the Word of God, visited the sick in our infirmary, lifted our minds and hearts to the Lord in our daily Eucharistic Liturgies - besides acting as Master of Ceremon.es at each and every function at our Molherhouse. For these wonderful years, all 17 of them, standing in cur sanctuary to praise God as a faithful steward, we are truly grateful to you. Father Charlie. He also served the needs of Vincenkan High School and loved assisting on weekends at St Thomas a Becket in Jefferson Boro and attended other local parish functions Father likewise participated in deanery activities in the North Hills area end meetings m the Diocese of Pittsburgh. Father Charlie knew how to blend work and leisure enjoying the best ol both — espeicaliy on the golf course. As recently as the Thursday before he died, he told Srsier Mary Clement and myself that, I ve lived life and I ve loved the file that I've lived. Whal more could I ask of GocP I am ready And he was ready to meet death as he met life with serenity, strength, simplicity, and peace. Father Charlie was not only our Chaplain - he was much more to us and to many other people He was both brother and friend This has been attested to over and over again in these past tew days as people shared with us their many beautiful life-giving and love giving memories of him Whenever he would preach a funeral liturgy lor one of our Sisters in lire Motherhouse Chapel, he was fond of recalling something speoaf about the de ceased Sister which would touch our hearts and help us to celebrate Ilie life lhal the Sister had offered as her unique gift to the community Whal is it that we best remember and chensn about our beloved Father McKoy? We remember his warm and bright smile, h,s witty comments, the fnendly wave of his hand in greeting, his kind words and his gentle concern about each per- son's well being and happiness We aiso remember this readiness to respond 10 any immediate needs, be it liturgical-sacramental, a visit to the hospital the lime he took to hsten and encourage - always affirming the best in each of us These were the very qualities which characterized him as pastoral presence io all. a very fine priest, one who represented Jesus to everyone whose He he touched Occasionally in his sermons Father McKoy would refer to his homeland — Ireland - as That Hite bit of lieaven on earth Of course, he was also known to say that he found "that little bit of heaven " on St Vincent FWI with the VSCs and he certainly brought "that hnie bit of heaven io us His casual express ons. his sense of humor, and his traditional St Patrick’s Day greeting — " The lop of the mornin" " — to all of us were evidence ol this. Ralph Waldo Emerson must have had Father Charlie in mind when he wrote the verse that appears on Father's memorial card "To laugh often and much; to win the respec! of intelligent people and the affection Of children, to earn the appreciation of honest critics and endure the betrayal : of false friends. Io aoprec ale beauty. Io find the best m others: to leave the world : a brt better whether by a healthy ch id, a garden patch, or a redeemed social con ! dition; to know even one life has breathed easier because I have lived This is to i have succeeded " The best legacy tnat Father McKoy has left us <s very amply - that he loved : us He will be sadly missed by all of our S sters. tne Precious Blood Congregation ’ by h>s brother. John, and ns family, h sSSter. A1 ce Ryan, and her femiy. h s relatives and his many, many friends As I recall him in Me and even now I think that what he would most want of us is to live as he lived - ' Life to the fullest and to love one another" Father Chartie. thank you tor a । you have been for us and have done tor us : You will live on in our hearts as a tne Chap’a n and as friend forever May you • rest m the Light of the Lord. Reactions to Bishop Korec’s Letter to Rude Pravo After finishing reading the Bishop Korec’s letter to Rude Pravo (Red Law) on the persecution of believers m Slovakia. I cannot remain silent When wifi the Slovak-Americans Such as Jednotari, Sokoli, Ligan and others let themselves be heard m mass protests against the religious and other human rights violations by the communist government in Slovakia and elsewhere? I asked myself and others so many times why we Slovak-Americans are so apathetic to the suffering and oppression ol our Christian brothers and sisters in Slovakia? I cannot find the nghl answer so far I can only speculate Can we call ourselves true Chnstians and Catholics and siiH not react and defend the God-given rights o' the people in the communist countries? Many Catholics naively support communist dictators of Nicaragua Do they noi know that communism is here first of all to destroy Christianity. Do they not know that since (he communists took power in Russia they have destroyed more 'han sixty-six million people, mostly Christians? Do Slovak-Americans not react to such horrible holocausts as the Cambodian one? Are our souls dead7 Are we waiting for our priests to lead us in the political and economic charge? Are we so conditioned as to leave ail the leadership to our priests7 That would be a tragedy. The priests cannot enter politics Why this passivism on Ihe side of the Slovak- Americans? Let us take a look at the Jews Look how well they defend their brothers and sisters all around the world. Cannot we do the same thing? When Ihe communists took power in Schem a. Moravia, and Slovakia in 19481 was eleven years old living m Bratislava At that time we had plenty of food and other bas e life necessities. One year later food disappeared from the stores, then airplanes, automobiles, shoes, bicycles, and even nails, and then in the mid-1950s everything became exoensive and unobtainable. Br 780 COMMITMENT By Rev. Thomas Andrew Doyle A Child’s Conscience Each generation wants their children to grow up and become good. healthy. and successful adults. But of course, before they reach those adult years, they progress through 20 or 25 years or so towards attaining a maturity and responsible level beneficial to them and society In that time span a vast amount of learning takes place w4h some of which results from outside sources while others fan within the parents control This latter area is the topic I am going to address today Last year, I came across an article by Ms Carol Bltss. a freelance writer, which focused upon 7 ways to develop a child's conscience Her topics were so important that I felt compelled to share them with you today I encourage you lo read them and hopefully incorporate them in your lives when con fronting situations like those listed below 1 Take control of TV watching 2 Substitute contemporary Christian music for rock music 3 Provide good books Don t assume a book from a library is good 4 Encourage your children s participation in church activities 5 Discuss issues like abortion, homosexuality, divorce, and other controversial topics before marriage 6 Teach children the right attitude towards work and money 7 Insist children keep the commitments they make Too many people today are trying to pass the buck and blame everyone else but themselves for how their children behave and turn out Sometimes, they are right but there are times when the parents are wrong Often, they do have a chance to actively and appropriately respond toward steering their children in the right direction instead of taking a passive tole and leaving the children respond to iheir own free will and choose for themselves. Next lime, think before you address those situations found above Would your guidance or decision benefit your children in the short term like Ihe near future and meet their immediate needs or m the long term like years down ihe road and help them become productive, God fearing and loving adults? tims are Ethiopia. Mozambique, and Nicaragua. But our media and many politicians do nol blame the communist government lor the hunger They blame the freedom lighters. Everyone should know by now lhal infamous instruction of Lenin to his party. "Hunger is a political tool. Using it we can manipulate any population to complete submisson To conclude this letter I ask every Catholic who reads Jednota lo cut out Bishop Korec s letter to Rude Pravo, add a leRer of protest of your own and mail them to your Congressman and to the president of Čzecho-Sovaka Hradčany. Prague This is the minimum we can do for our oppressed brothers and sisters of Slovakia in our sti i-free Amenca But there is more we can do. Bishop Korec, and his life, and send it to every Catholic bishop and politician in the United States and Canada it should also be sent to every Sunday school. O'Byrne, refigion will have a less prominent bld official place al the modern Winter Olympics in Calgary as well. Bishop O'Byme, who heads the Calgary Diocese, chairs an ecumenical Olympic committee seeking to promote Olympic values and provide a religious presence for both athletes and spectators For the athletes, that means access to the clergy from the Univer síly of Calgary's campus ministry and local churches serving as chaplains at the villages housing teams For the tounsts. lhal means the hospitality offered by an ecumenical center served by volunteers Irorn local congregations who can steer outsiders toward the church services ol thar choice or find help in addressing other needs. In adefton. Bishop O’Byme explaned Feb. 9 in a telephone interview with National Catholic News Service, the corp- rrdtee is "helping make known Ihe base values of the Olympic concept." which could get overlooked in all the competition He said such values include the ideas that Ihe Olympics stand for "develop- men! of athletes' skills in al ways. . that the spirit of good sportsmanship" prevails, that respect for ail athletes and their abilities is encouraged, and "that winning is not the only ihing." His committee, which consists of a core panel of about 15 clergy and subcommittees of many more to oversee various aspects ol the Olympics, "touches all churches functioning in the Calgary region," he said. It has drawn support from such , diverse groups as Moslems, Jews. ' j Sikhs, Buddhists and members ol the Bahai community, as well as ihe more established Catholic and other Christian congregations, the bishop said The committee, an official part ol the Olympic organization, is the first Of its type, the bishop said An ecumenical service Jan. 31. held in an indoor hockey rink, featured prayers by leaders from the various faiths, hymns and singing, personal remarks by athletes who are religious believers, candle-lighting, and "a little hockey game — yes, as part of the service.” Bishop O'Byrne said The latter involved 5- to 7-year-old &" skaters. "The object was to show that v these are youngsters growing up and benefiting from the spirit generated by ihe Olympics.” the txshop said- A major purpose ol Ihe service was ""io indicate that the values ol the Olympics and the values of the church, ol religion, were able lo blend very well." he said. With that goal continuing, "Ihe next couple of weeks it s going to be pretty busy." he said. He said that one of his main duties is "to visit the villages and be supportive ol the chaplains." The chaplains' role "is kind ol an important one because Ihe athletes are so ŕ keyed up" and may need readily available counseling to help cope with stress, he said. It an athlete asks a chaplain to pray for his or her victory over other competitors. ihe dilemma will be similar io ihat confronted by a bishop when two Catholic schools compete in football. Bishop O’Byrne noted. '11 just wonder what confusion they’re making in heaven,” he quipped. Faced wilh such an athlete’s request, headded. Td say. Box 6965, GCPO, Now York, NY 10163-6026 ___ 4 [pageend14]SVÄTÝ METOD JEDNOTA. WEDNESDAY. FEBRUARY 17. 1988 Page 15 DAR BOŽÍ SKRZ 25 ROKOV Milnn S. fhirlca, PhD. Nie je vždy ľahko byť súrodencom nadpriemernej, vynikajúcej osobnosti. Alebo sa taký brat stane žiarlivým sokom génia, čo ho môže priviesť až ku kainovskému komplexu, a- lebo rezignuje pred nedosiahnuteľnou veľkosťou brata a stane sa mu tieňom, pomocníkom, nástrojom bez vlastnej osobnosti. Obidvom z týchto extrémnych úskalí vedel sa vyhnúť Metod zo Solúna. Ani on neprišiel na svet bez hojných darov ducha i tela. Syn vysokého cisárskeho dôstojníka, prejavil nevšedné nadanie a vyštudoval rímske právo v samom Carihrade. Nemal ani tridsať rokov, keď dosiahol vysoký úrad cisárskeho miestodržiteľa. No po desaťročnej službe utiahol sa z funkčne a vstúpi! do kláštora, aby slúžil len Pánu Bohu. Zatiaľ najmladší z jeho šiestich súrodencov, Konštantín, urobil závratnú kariéru ako vedec: absolvoval s takým úspechom všetky vedné discipliny, ktoré sa prednášali na cisárskych školách v Carihrade, že bol vyznačený najprednej- ším titulom “Filozof. Keď od- Sv&tý Otec Ján Pavo! n. káže po slovensky v kaplnke Slovenského ústavu, sv. Cyrila a Metoda v Ríme, dún 8. novembra 1981. Spomienka 1,100 výročie smrti sv. Metoda. Velehrad, Júl 1985. — Snímka: Otec Juraj Rybanský. Svätý Metod mietol ponúkané mu výhodné manželstvo a vysoké funkcie na cisárskom dvore, prijal len úrad riaditeľa patriarchálnej knižnice a funkciu profesora na cisárskej vysokej škole. Ale čoskoro aj on prišiel na myšlienku utiahnuť sa do kláštora a zaklopal na brány Olympu, kde sa medzitým jeho brat Metod stal opátom. Cisársky dvor sa však nechcel celkom zrieknuť takého vynikajúceho talentu. Cisár Michal HL poveroval svojho niekdajšieho spolužiaka Konštantína najdelikátnejšími diplomatickými misiami u blízkych i ďalekých národov, pričom viac- ráz mu pridelil aj Metoda ako pomocníka. Tak to bolo aj v roku 863, keď sa Michal III. rozhodol vyhovieť žiadosti Rastislava a poslať mu učiteľa, ktorý by Slovákom vysvetlil kresťanské pravdy v ich vlastnom jazyku. Prvé tri roky účinkovania byzantských bratov v moravskom kráľovstve Slovákov o Metodovi sa málo hovorilo a písalo. On vedel prijať skromnú funkciu pomocníka a pracoval akoby v tieni svojho mladšieho brata. Všetky veľké podnikania toho času: preklady najzákladnejších kníh do starej slovenčiny, školenie kandidátov na kňazstvc .príprava na cestu do Ríma a s ňou spojené dôležité udalosti — všetko sa pripisovalo Konštantínovi. Ale keď si Pán Boh nečakane povolal do večnosti sotva 40-ročného Filozofa, hneď sa ukázalo, že skromný mních Metod nebol iba tieňom svojho geniálneho brata. Musel už aj v Ríme zapôsobiť tým najlepším dojmom, keď ho pápež Hadrian II. vysvätil hneď za panónskeho arcibiskupa a navyše ho ešte vymenoval za svojho legáta pre všetky slovanské národy. Išlo o celkom mimoriadny postup zo strany Svätej Stolice ,ktorá v týchto veciach nikdy sa príliš nenáhli. Na porovnanie stačí si spomenúť, že napríklad Česi, ak prijmeme za isté, že Metod pokrstil ich knieža Bořivoja niekedy v polovici sedemdesiatych rokov IX. storočia, dosiahli zriadenie biskupstva v Prahe až v roku 973 (teda o celých sto rokov neskôr); a na vlastné arcibiskupstvo museli čakať až do roku 1344. Alt sa teda prvému slovenskému arcibiskupovi podarilo za krátky čas pätnástich rokov jeho činnosti uprostred starých Slovákov dosiahnuť nielen zriadenie samostatného arcibiskupstva v ich sídelnom meste Morave, ale aj dvoch ďalších biskupských sídiel — o Nitre sa zachovali jasné dokumenty; to druhé bolo asi v Koceľovom kniežatstve alebo v Malopoľaku — svedči to o jeho celkom nevšednej veľkosti tak ako veľkňaza apoštolských kvalít, aj ako výtečného organizátora cirkevných inštitúcií. Casto sa však pritom zabúda, že sv. Metod mal levský podiel aj na organizovaní štátnej správy v rapídne sa rozpínajúcej ríši Svätopluka, a najmä na povznesení a upevnení jej medzinárodného postavenia. Veď už v roku 879 pápež Ján VTTT vyznačil Svätopluka prestížnym titulom “syna sv. Petra" a o rok neskôr povýšil ho dokonca na “jediného syna", ktorému ríšu prijal pod priamu ochranu apoštola sv. Petra a jeho nástupcov. To znamenalo nielen uznanie kráľovskej hodnosti a moci slovenského vlá- dara najvyššou autoritou vtedajšieho sveta, ale mohlo byť tiež prejavom diplomaticky naznačenej možnosti zveriť tomuto “jedinému synovi” aj korunu Rímskeho cisárstva. Nemožno si predstaviť, ako by boh mohli pápeži poctiť kráľa Svätopluka takými nevšednými privilégiami bez toho, žeby sa o to zasadil plnou váhou svojej autority a vybrúseným taktom svojho diplomatického umenia práve arcibiskup a pápežský legát Metod. Keď Metod cítil, že už a j jemu prichádza čas zakončiť pozemské putovanie — veď sa dožil na oné časy naozaj patriarchálneho veku! — chcel čo najlepšie zabezpečiť budú cnosť svojho diela. Zvolal preto kňazskú synodu a vymenoval za svojho nástupcu slovenského kňaza (alebo už biskupa?) Go- razda. Potom požehnal kráľa, duchovenstvo i všetok veriaci ľud n odovzdal dušu svojmu Stvoriteľovi. Pochovali ho spievajúc v troch jazykoch, v ktorých tento veľký Človek, svätý kňaz a neohrozený apoštol žil, myslel, učil a kázal; latinsky, grécky a slovensky. V roku 1936 počas španielskej revolúcie, aj počas II. svetovej vojny, až po dnešnú dobu, sv. Cirkev utrpela na strate kňazov, rehoľníkov a rehoľ- nie. Všade sa vypráva a cíti pokles povoláni na stav kňazský, aj rehoľný. Lež tu v Indii je to akási výnimka, táto kríza je menšia než na Západe (v Európe). Je pravda, že počas TI. svetovej vojny, veľa misionárov, jak Taliani ako aj Nemci boli tu sústredení v táboroch za plných 6 rokov, a po vojne, viacerí museli opustiť toto územie navždy a noví misionári cudzinci nemajú povolené prísť cem až do teraz Lež ako vždycky... keď je núdza najväčšia... pomoc Božia najbližšia. Z južnej čiastky Indie, zvlášť zo štátu Kerala, došli chlapci jak k saleziánom, tak aj do biskupských seminárov; a výsledky sa ukázali u- spokojivé. Keď na začiatku roku 1922. prví 11. saleziáni došli do Shil- longu, hlavného mesta vtedajšieho Assamu (teraz rozdelený na viac menších štátov, a Meghalaya je jeden z nich), tak saleziáni d o s t ali Apoštolskú Prefektúru, z 5 tisíc katolíkov a dva tisíc katechumenov roztrúsených po vtedajšom Assa- me. — A teraz? Shillong je ar- cibiakupstvo a ďalších sedem biskupstiev; a katolíkov máme hlhko jeden milión. Päť biskupov je zo saleziánskych semi- nirov-ašpírantov. Tiež traja biskupi sú svetskí a ostatní sú saleziáni. Savio Junioráte je saleziánsky ašpirant. Práve pred mesiacom sme oslavovali 25. výročie založenia tohoto ústavu. Za týchto 25 rokov prešlo ústavom 1582 chlapcov-ašpirantov. Viarcrí necítili povolanie stať sa kňazmi-saleziánmi. Niektorí šli do biskupského seminára a- lebo do inej rehole. Za 25 rokov apoštolskej práce je 124 vysvätených kňazov, ďalej teraz máme 139 klerikov, z ktorých istý počet bude vysvätených za kňazov v blízkej budúcnosti Ďalších 5 saleziánskych bratov-re- hoľníkov Spolu 268 seleziá- nov. Tento školský rok tu máme 183 ašpirantov vo 4. triedach, všetci z rozdielnych kmeňov iba tejto čiastky Indie. Ďalších 90 ašpirantov študentov kolégia v Rongkhon, Garo Hills, a 33 novicov. Všetky tri kategórie sú bývali študenti tohoto ústavu. — Mimo týchto troch skupín, máme ešte 29 študentov kolégia, z nich niekoľko reme- aeľníkov v meste Shillong. Tak z tejto príležitosti sa ob- 36. Otec superior mi prichádza v ústrety. Reku, čo sa stalo, drahý otče! On mi pomaly vysvetľuje, že v blízkej dedinke Lúpia je akýsi veľký had na strome, a to v samej dedine Ľudia už od rána tu na mňa čakajú. Domáci poľovníci ho vraj nemôžu zabiť alebo skôr sa ho boja, či by som nešiel s nimi, lebo ináč tu ešte budú čakať celú noc. Sú celkom presvedčení, že je to zlý duch, čo sa na nich prišiel pomstiť za to, že sú kresťania. Môj príchod ich veľmi potešil. Pozdravovali ma podľa svojej obyčaje, ako najlepšie vedeli. Naozaj tam bol veľký suchý strom a medzi konármi bol skrútený had. akého som ešte nevidel. Pane Bože, len aby som ho dobre trafil! Pozeral som, kde má hlavu. Všetci mlčali, bolo ticho ako v hrobe. Všetky biele oči na čiernych tvárach boli upreté na mňa. Nabil som pušku silným nábojom. Prežehnal som sa a už len čakám, aby som si nabral trocha vzduchu a aby som sa trocha upokojil. No reku už môžem. Priložím pušku k zapotenému lícu, pomaly mierim a konečne bác, veľká rana. Čakáme, čo bude. O niekoľko sekúnd sa zachveli konáre a s veľkým rachotom sa zrútil obrovský had s rozbitou hlavou. Bolo to radosti a kriku "NGwere", až sa tak ozývalo celým okolím. Černosi ozbrojení kopijami ho chceli dopichať a posekať na kúsky, ale ja som im zastal cestu. Vravím: “Ja som ho zabil, či nie? Teda patrí mne!’ 'Dvaja silní černosi si ho uviazali na dlhy drúk a odniesli sme bo do misie. Tam ho znovu obdivovali školské deti a všetci obyvatelia misie. Po všetkých ceremóniách prišiel rad na mňa. Stiahol som z neho kožu a pekne som ju vysušil. Koža bez hlavy bola dlhá 20 stôp (vj’še šesť metrov) a široká jeden a pol stopy (necelého pol metra). Táto koža je teraz v misijnom múzeu v Chicagu (v USA), kam ju odniesla jedna zo sestričiek, keď bola na návšteve tu u nás v Afrike. Teda aj takéto prípad y sa vyskytnú a aj takto sa pomáha našim čiernym, keď je to potrebné. SINÁKOVÁ (Pokračovanie) Rehoľnice-mučenice Keď Dávid s Katkou ostali sami doma, Katka ho prekvapila otázkou: “Oi fli 84 naozaj rozhodol kúpiť ten dom?” “Rozhodne, áno!" Prekvapene hradel na nu a pýtal sa: "Drahá,. čo ti to zase prebehlo hlavičkou ?” ■ ^'K&tí^-nnberíic odvahy, prosebným hlasom hovorí: ^-T^WemaTby si ešte trocha čakať s tou kúpou? Myslím, máme tu dosť miesta. Mama a otecko si želajú, aby sme s nimi boli aspoň do Vianoc." "Do Vianoc!" Dávid opakoval, skúmavým zrakom merajúc Katku, pýtal sa: "Povedz mi úprimne pravdu, či to len preto navrhuješ, že rodičia sa tak vyslovili ? Ja myslím, že lepšie bude, keď pôjdeme na svoje. Takto budeme pevnejšia rodina, vzácnejší jeden druhému. Takto nám často mama hovorievala. Jej sa bude vraj cnieť? Veď tak hovoria všetky matky o svojich deťoch, ako by z obyčaje. Však ešte traja ostanú doma." "Nehovor tak, Dávid," napomínala ho. “Nebuďme nemilosrdní. Naša matka robi výnimku. Ja cítim, že predsa by sme mali ostať." A ako keby ho prosila: "Veronka je von z domu; otecko nebude môcť pracovať; hádam až niekedy na jar bude na niečo schopný." Prikl'akla k nemu: "Aspoň dnes sa nerozhodni, čakaj do zajtra alebo aspoň do nedele. Uvidíš, ako sa otecko bude cítit Keby som ťa prosila, či ani kvôli mne by si neostal doma? Mne by sa páčilo, keby sme ostali doma do jari. Zima aj tak rýchlo ubehne." Teraz sa jej odľahčilo na srdci, že sa mu s jej plánom zdôverila. "Keby otecko nepracoval päť alebo i desať rokov, aj tak majú z čoho žiť,” odpovedal nakrátko a bezstarostne Dávid. "Nemyslím tu na peniaze. Ale všimni si, náhodou by sa aj Milka vydala, veľký dom by ostal prázdny, zo všetkých izieb by vyzerala samota. Viem, že tým by sa oteckovi na zdraví nezlepšilo." Dávid sa pozrel na Katku celý zadivený. "Ešte mi aj tretiu svadbu prorokuješ. Závdavok na dom päťsto dolárov už máme tu. Oddnes za týždeň budeme mať všetko kúpené. Už ma aj tak volajú do práce. Ale týždeň ešte vystanem." "Prečo by som nemohla prorokovať svadbu? Milka nám neostane dlho doma, preto ešte raz ťa prosím, dočkaj aspoň do nedele. Nevieš, či sa oteckovi nezhorši. A ja by som najradšej ostala tu." Hľadala slová, ktorými by ho mohla odhovoriť od jeho rozhodnutia. "Všimni si, ako mi je tu dobre, veselo. Máme sa s kým zhová- rat S Julkou a Dankom mám školu angličtiny. Tam budem osamote. Nemysli, že by som sa obávala, ale predsa.. "Moja drahá, viem ako je to byť nevestou. Ty ňou nemusíš byť. Pôjdeme preč, zakiaľ si ešte vzácna. Budeš paňou vo vlastnom dome. Povedz mi otvorene, či sa ti ten dom nepáči, ktorý som vyhľadal? A keď sa ti zdá odtiaľ ďaleko do mesta, kúpime dom bližšie." Chcejúc Katku vyhovoriť o tej "samote", tešil ju: "Vieš, aby sa ti nenudilo, naučím ťa šoférovať. Kedy sa ti zapáči, pôjdeš navštíviť rodičov. Nože, prečo máš mať taký smutný výraz na tvári? Ukáž, či sa vieš usmievať. Ja som dosiaľ nepočul nevesty tak hovoriť, lebo obyčajne každá túži za svojou vlastnou domácnosťou. Ty si celkom opačného zjnýšľania. Veronka bude pod- istým za nevestu, lenže jej svokra bude bývať v inom štáte. Ale ty by ai mala svokru na krku každý deň, vždy by si sa musela ohliadať, aby si niečo neurobila proti vôli domácich. Rozumej mi: Ja milujem matku. A čo ti hovorím, nemysli si, že tým myslím niečo zlého o matke. Bože zachovaj! Veď je prirodzené, že byť za nevestu, nie je to tak. ako keby si bola vo svojom dome a mala svoju vlastnú domácnost Azda mi len dáš za pravdu?" “Nuž, vo všeobecnosti je to tak, ale nie v tomto našom prípade. Ja vydržím byť tou nevestou aspoň do jari. A bolo by to i pre mňa výhodnejšie, lebo večerami by som mohla navštevovať školu. Uznáš, že mám pravdu?" Katka zamyslene odpovedala. "Poddávam sa, aspoň nateraz." Dávid bol dojatý jej láskou k jeho rodičom. Vrelo ju bozkal. "Aby si nemyslela, že som tvrdohlavý, dočkám s rozhodnutím do nedele, keď ti to urobí radosť.” "Dávid, ty zlatý Dávid,” ľúbostné zašeptala a objala manžela. "Do nedele vec dobre uvážiš." Nevedela sa pretvárať s jej horúcou láskou k nemu. Radovala sa a preto mu to aj tak srdečne vyslovila. “Teraz mám naozaj dušu na mieste. Kde teraz pôjdeme ? Cí chceš ostať doma? Kedy pôjdeme do nemocnice?" “Najprv idem obzrieť auto. A keď sa vrátim, poviem ti, kam pôjdeme. Musím ti vyznať, že ťa obdivujem. Ktorá iná nevesta by tak s radosťou chcela ísť navštíviť chorého svokra do nemocnice?” A doložil: "Ty malá šelmička! Ký div, že píšeš romány a novely. Vieš, ktorou strunou ťahať, aby si mohla svojho manžela okrútiť okolo prsta. Ty si ozaj zradená herečka," a sladko ju vybozkával. Dávid videl v Katke anjela. Ona sa nevie pretvarovať. Vedela si ho plne získať. A on by jej bol zniesol nebo k nohám. Ako by teda nevyhovel jej žiadosti? Keď nadišla nedeľa, Dávid vedel, že všetko ostane tak, ako TUZEX zasielame bezpečne a rýchlo UROBTE RADOST RODINKE A ZNÁMYM V STAROM KRAJI. PENIAZE Z DEDIČSTVA POSIELAME TIEŽ V PLNEJ HODNOTE.
